❯                                                                               
  You're going to help me build the Phase 1 frontend for **Fyntra**, an         
  RFID-based school attendance and child-safety platform for Pakistani schools. 
   The full product context, scope, data models, and conventions live in        
  `README.md`.                                                                  
                                                                                
  ## Before you write any code                                                  
                                                                                
  1. **Read `README.md` in full.** Don't skim. Pay particular attention to      
  sections 2 (scope), 4 (directory structure), 5 (data models), 6 (API          
  contract), 9 (edge cases), and 13 (hardware reality).                         
  2. **Summarize back to me in 6–10 bullets** what you understood: the product, 
   the three roles, the Phase 1 scope, and anything that feels ambiguous or     
  under-specified. Flag every ambiguity explicitly — don't paper over it.       
  3. **Propose a build sequence.** Default I expect:                            
     1. Project bootstrap (Vite + TS strict + Tailwind + RTL plugin + ESLint +  
  Prettier)                                                                     
     2. Providers, router, i18n config, Tailwind theme tokens                   
     3. The first 5–6 atoms (Button, Input, Badge, Avatar, Spinner, Icon) with  
  tests                                                                         
     4. MSW setup, seed data, and Zod schemas forata models                     
     5. Auth flow end-to-end (request OTP → verify → store token → redirect by  
  role)                                                                         
     6. **Parent home, end-to-end with mocked data** — login → home → child     
  timeline. One vertical slice working before going wide.                       
     7. Admin dashboard skeleton, then fill out students / cards / devices /    
  reports                                                                       
     8. Teacher view                                                            
     9. Notification settings + log                                             
     10. Polish, a11y pass, RTL pass with one Urdu screenshot                   
  4. **Wait for my go-ahead** before generating files. I'd rather agree on the  
  plan than re-do work.                                                         
                                                                                
  ## Working style I want                                                       
                                                                                
  - **Build vertical slices, not horizontal layers.** Get *one* parent flow     
  working end-to-end with mocks before scaffolding 30 half-built screens. The   
  first demo-able milestone is: I can log in as a parent on my phone, see       
  today's status for one child, and tap into a 30-day timeline.                 
  - **Every new component gets a basic test alongside it.** Render test         
  minimum; behavior tests where it matters (Button onClick, Form submission,    
  etc.).                                                                        
  - **Atomic design discipline.etching in atoms or molecules. Organisms own the 
   Query consumers. Pages are thin.                                             
  - **No barrel files (`index.ts` re-exports) anywhere.** Import from the       
  source file directly.                                                         
  - **Validate API responses with Zod** before they touch React Query state.    
  - **Stop and ask** when you hit a real ambiguity. Don't invent assumptions    
  silently — call them out so we can decide together.                           
  - **Commit after every meaningful slice** with a clear message. Don't pile    
  multiple concerns into one commit.                                            
                                                                                
  ## A couple of things I care about up front                                   
                                                                                
  - **The simulator matters.** I already have a USB RFID reader and test cards. 
   The "Simulate Tap" panel (admin → devices) needs to capture real reader      
  input (most USB RFID readers act as keyboards) so I can demo with actual      
  hardware against the mock backend. See README §13.                            
  - **Bilingual is real, not cosmetic.** Don't hardcode English strings         
  expecting to swap them later. Use i18n keys from day one. Set up `dir="rtl"`  
  switching as part of the layout, not as a Phase 2 retrofit.                   
  -  parent home screen sets the tone for the whole product.** It should feel   
  calm, reassuring, and answer one question loudly: *"Is my child at school     
  right now?"* When you build it, treat it as the hero of the app.              
                                                                                
  When you're ready, start with step 1 above — read the README, then summarize  
  back. I'll respond before you write any code.

⏺ I've read the README in full. Before I write anything, here's what I
  understood plus the ambiguities I want to resolve with you.

  What I understood

  - Product. RFID gate-tap attendance for small/medium private schools in
  Lahore, sold as child-safety to parents and ops-relief to principals. The
  emotional center is the parent home screen answering one question: "Is my 
  child at school right now?"
  - Three roles, three shapes. Parent = mobile-first PWA-ish, OTP login. Admin =
   desktop, dense tables, live tap feed, devices, cards, reports. Teacher =
  desktop/tablet, roster-for-today with manual override.
  - Mocked backend in Phase 1. MSW serves the API in §6 against seed data (1
  school, 4 classes, 60 students, 2 devices). Polling at 15s through a
  useRealtime abstraction so it can become WebSockets in Phase 2 without
  rewriting consumers.
  - Bilingual is structural, not cosmetic. English + Urdu, RTL via Tailwind's
  RTL plugin, Noto Nastaliq Urdu font, document dir driven by locale, all copy
  via i18n keys from day one. Canonical timezone Asia/Karachi, phone numbers
  stored E.164, displayed local.
  - Atomic design with hard rules. Atoms presentational, organisms own Query,
  pages thin. No barrel files anywhere. Zod-validate every API response before
  it touches Query. Co-located tests. Tests are mandatory per component.
  - Edge cases are the spec. Card-not-assigned ≠ absent; device-offline =
  "unverified" not "absent"; same-direction taps within 30s = dedupe; in/out
  within 60s = flag for review; manual overrides always carry who/what/when/why
  with required reason; multi-school parent = error, don't guess.
  - Hardware reality. USB RFID readers act as keyboards. The admin "Simulate
  Tap" page needs a focus-capturing input so a real reader can drive POST 
  /dev/simulate-tap against MSW. This is the only physical-hardware integration
  point in Phase 1.
  - Visual posture. Calm neutral palette, soft green for present, muted amber
  for late, deep red reserved strictly for genuine alarms. "One number per
  screen" on parent home — not a dashboard.

  Ambiguities I want to resolve before coding

  1. Auth contradiction — biggest one. §6's API has only /auth/request-otp +
  /auth/verify-otp, but §7 says admin login is "email/phone + password." Either
  (a) all roles use OTP and §7's wording is loose, or (b) we need a /auth/login
  password endpoint for admin/teacher. I'd prefer (a) — OTP for everyone in 
  Phase 1 (one auth flow to build, one to test). OK?
  2. How does a parent find their kids? /me returns a User, but there's no GET 
  /students?guardianId=me in the contract. Phase 1 needs that, or we extend /me
  to include children: Student[]. Propose: GET /students?guardianId=me.
  3. Timeline endpoint shape. GET /students/:id/timeline?from=&to= — does it
  return AttendanceRecord[] (day rows) or TapEvent[] (raw events) or both? §7
  implies day-summary in the list and events on tap. Propose: timeline returns
  AttendanceRecord[], and tapping a day fetches GET 
  /tap-events?studentId=&from=&to= for that day. OK?
  4. What's the "absent" cutoff? If the device is online and the school day has
  started, when do we flip a kid from "no tap yet" to "absent"? Not specified.
  Propose: school.startTime + lateThresholdMinutes + 60min = absent. Worth
  confirming.
  5. Notification settings shape. PATCH /notifications/settings { channels, 
  events } — the inner shape isn't defined. Propose enumerating: channels: { 
  whatsapp, sms, in_app } and events: { tap_in, tap_out, late, manual_override, 
  device_offline }, all booleans. Plus a language: 'en' | 'ur'. OK?
  6. Polling lifecycle. 15s is fine during school hours, wasteful after endTime.
   Propose useRealtime pauses outside [startTime-30min, endTime+30min] and on
  tab blur. Confirm?
  7. Bootstrap reality. The repo is already initialized with React 19 (not 18 as
   the README says), Vite 8, TS 6, react-compiler. Tailwind, Router, Query, MSW,
   Zustand, i18next, Vitest are not installed. I'd keep React 19 (it works with
  everything we need) and update the README's stack line later. Also: directory
  is not a git repo (.gitignore exists but no .git). Should I git init as part
  of step 1 so we can commit per slice?
  8. PWA scope. §2 says "PWA-ready" but push is stubbed. Propose: install
  vite-plugin-pwa with a minimal manifest + offline shell, no push wiring. Or
  defer entirely. Your call.

  Proposed build sequence

  Your 10-step plan is good. I'd adjust step 1 and split step 6 to make the
  first demo-able milestone explicit:

  1. Install missing deps + configure (Tailwind v3 + RTL plugin, RR v6, TanStack
   Query v5, Zustand, RHF + Zod, react-i18next, date-fns + date-fns-tz, MSW v2,
  Lucide, Recharts, Vitest + RTL + jsdom + MSW node, Prettier + ESLint rules).
  git init. Verify dev, build, test, lint all run on an empty shell.
  2. Providers + router + i18n + theme tokens. App.tsx mounts
  QueryClientProvider, I18nextProvider, router, locale-driven dir. Tailwind
  tokens: neutral grays, soft green, muted amber, deep red as semantic names.
  3. First 6 atoms with tests. Button, Input, Badge, Avatar (with initials
  fallback), Spinner, Icon. Co-located .test.tsx. No barrel files.
  4. MSW + seed + Zod schemas. All types from §5 get Zod schemas in
  types/schemas.ts. Seed services/mocks/seed.ts deterministic. Handlers cover
  every endpoint in §6 with realistic latency.
  5. Auth flow end-to-end. Request OTP → verify OTP → token in Zustand
  (persisted) → redirect by role. Zod-validated response. Bilingual login screen
   as the first real RTL test.
  6. Vertical slice: Parent Home + Timeline. Login as parent → see today's
  status hero card per child → tap into 30-day timeline → tap a day → see that
  day's tap events. Loading, error, empty, "no card assigned", "device offline =
   unverified" states all handled. This is the first demo.
  7. Admin shell + Dashboard. Layout, nav, stat cards, live tap feed, device
  status row. Polling via useRealtime.
  8. Admin sub-pages. Students list/detail, Cards
  (assign/replace/lost/deactivate with audit), Devices grid + Simulate Tap with 
  USB reader capture, Reports (range picker + CSV), Notifications log.
  9. Teacher view. My class today (roster + manual override with required
  reason), class history.
  10. Notification settings + log polish. Channel/event matrix + language
  toggle.
  11. A11y + RTL pass. Keyboard nav, focus rings, contrast, one Urdu screenshot
  of parent home as the acceptance shot.

  Commit at the end of each step (and after the auth slice and parent home slice
   specifically — those are demo-able moments).

  Waiting for your go-ahead before I touch any files. Answer the eight
  ambiguities above (even briefly — "1a, 2 yes, 3 yes, 4 yes, 5 yes, 6 yes, 7
  init git + keep React 19, 8 defer PWA" works) and I'll start with step 1.

✻ Baked for 1m 22s

❯ Your 10-step plan is good, but please check the detailed answers to your      
  ambiguities: These are genuinely good questions. Here are my answers, in      
  order, so you can paste them straight back.                                   
                                                                                
  **1. Auth — go with (a), OTP for everyone.** One flow to build, one to test,  
  and OTP is already the default mental model in Pakistan (Careem, Foodpanda,   
  banks, JazzCash all do OTP). The §7 wording was loose — treat OTP as          
  canonical, delete the password mention.                                       
                                                                                
  **2. How parents find their kids — extend `/me`.** Make `/me` return `{ user, 
   children: Student[] }` when the user is a parent. The parent home loads on   
  every app open; saving a round trip there matters more than purity. Also keep 
   `GET /students?guardianId=me` available for refetch scenarios, but `/me` is  
  the primary path.                                                             
                                                                                
  **3. Timeline shape — agree exactly with the proposal.** `GET                 
  /students/:id/timeline` returns `AttendanceRecord[]` (day summaries for the   
  calendar). Tapping a day calls `GET /tap-events?studentId=&from=&to=` scoped  
  to that single day. That matches how parents actually use it — overview       
  first, drill in on curio Absent cutoff — I'd refine the proposal.** The       
  current framing conflates two things that should be separate:                 
     - **Attendance status** (data): `late` from `startTime`, `absent` from     
  `startTime + absentThresholdMinutes`                                          
     - **Parent alert** (notification): fires when child crosses into `absent`  
                                                                                
     Add a new field `absentThresholdMinutes` to the `School` entity (default   
  `30`). Don't reuse `lateThresholdMinutes + 60` — that puts the "your child    
  hasn't arrived" alert at ~9:00 AM, which is way too late. Schools start at    
  7:45, and a parent who learns at 9 AM that their kid never arrived will be    
  furious. 30 minutes is the right ballpark.                                    
                                                                                
  **5. Notification settings shape — agree with one tweak.** Use Claude Code's  
  proposal, but:                                                                
     - `language` does *not* belong here — it's already on                      
  `User.preferredLanguage` and it affects the whole UI, not just notifications  
     - Add `absent` to the events list (the high-priority "child not arrived"   
  alert from #4)                                                                
     - For parents, exclude `device_offline` from th they can subscribe to —    
  that's an admin/teacher concern only                                          
                                                                                
  **6. Polling lifecycle — full agreement.** Pause outside `[startTime - 30min, 
   endTime + 30min]` and on tab blur. Also use the Page Visibility API to pause 
   when the tab is hidden but technically focused (background tab on mobile).   
  React Query's `refetchOnWindowFocus` handles part of this for free.           
                                                                                
  **7. Bootstrap reality — keep React 19, do git init, update the README.**     
  React 19 + Vite 8 + TS 6 is fine for everything in our stack. Yes, `git init` 
   as part of step 1 and commit per vertical slice — that's the only way the    
  "stop and ask when ambiguous" discipline works (we need to be able to revert  
  cleanly). Tell Claude Code to commit the README update ("React 19, not 18")   
  as the first commit so we have a clean history.                               
                                                                                
  **8. PWA scope — install `vite-plugin-pwa` with a minimal manifest, no        
  push.** Worth it for two reasons: the parent demo feels much more real if a   
  principal can "Add to Home Screen" on the spot, and the manifest forces you   
  on app name, icon, and theme color early (which is good design discipline).   
  Skip the service worker beyond a basic offline shell. Push notifications stay 
   stubbed.                                                                     
                                                                                
  ---                                                                           
                                                                                
  **update the README in the repo with these decisions** before moving on.      
  Right now the README is the source of truth, and if these answers only live   
  in chat history, the next session will re-litigate them. Commit the README    
  updates as the first commit, then proceed to scaffolding.

      269  **Real-time strategy for Phase 1.** Poll the relevant endpoint

      270  
      271 +**Polling lifecycle.** `useRealtime` is the *only* place this 
          +logic lives — consumers pass a channel and forget about it.   
      272 +- Active window: `[school.startTime − 30min, school.endTime + 
          +30min]` in `Asia/Karachi`. Outside the window, polling pauses 
          +entirely.                                                     
      273 +- Tab visibility: when `document.visibilityState !== "visible"
          +` (Page Visibility API), polling pauses. Resumes on visibility
          + change.                                                      
      274 +- Window focus: React Query's `refetchOnWindowFocus: true` han
          +dles the "user came back to the tab" refresh — we don't need t
          +o duplicate that.                                             
      275 +- This avoids draining batteries on phones left open after pic
          +kup and silences pointless background traffic.

      271 -**Polling lifecycle.** `useRealtime` is the *only* place this 
          -logic lives — consumers pass a channel and forget about it.   
      272 -- Active window: `[school.startTime − 30min, school.endTime + 
          -30min]` in `Asia/Karachi`. Outside the window, polling pauses 
          -entirely.

          -` (Page Visibility API), polling pauses. Resumes on visibility
          - change.

          -dles the "user came back to the tab" refresh — we don't need t

  Two decisions I made unilaterally that are worth a quick gut-check before I 
  proceed:

  1. .npmrc with legacy-peer-deps=true. react-i18next@15 declares peerOptional 
  typescript@"^5" but the project is on TS 6. Since the peer is optional and has
   no runtime impact, I told npm to accept it project-wide rather than downgrade
   TS. Alternative would have been to pin TS to 5.x.
  2. Bumped Vitest 2 → 4 and vite-plugin-pwa 0.20 → 1. Their older majors cap at
   Vite 5; the project is on Vite 8. No way around this without downgrading
  Vite.

  Both have brief justifications in the commit message.

❯                                                                               
                                                                                
  Before step 2, a hardware decision changed: we're using an **ACR122U** (ACS   
  PC/SC NFC reader) for Phase 1, not a keyboard-emulation reader. The reader    
  does not type into text fields — it speaks PC/SC. The integration approach in 
   the README's §13 is therefore wrong as written and must be updated before    
  any UI work begins that depends on it.                                        
                                                                                
  Don't proceed to step 2 yet. Do this first:                                   
                                                                                
  ## What to update in `README.md`                                              
                                                                                
  ### 1. Replace §13 entirely with this new content:                            
                                                                                
  ```markdown                                                                   
  ## 13. The hardware reality                                                   
                                                                                
  The reader for Phase 1 is an **ACR122U** (ACS, USB NFC reader, PC/SC          
  standard). It does *not* emulate a keyboard — it speaks the PC/SC protocol    
  and is accessed through the operating system's smart-card framework           
  (`CryptoTokenKit` on macOS, `pcscd` on Linux, WinSCard on Windows). Card UIDs 
   cannot be obtained by capturing keyboard input.                              
                                                                                
  To bridge the reader to the frontend during development, Phase 1 includes a   
  small **local-only bridge service** alongside the frontend, in its own        
  subdireof the repo:                                                           
                                                                                
  ```                                                                           
  fyntra/                                                                       
  ├── src/        # frontend (existing app)                                     
  └── bridge/     # local-only Node service: ACR122U → WebSocket → frontend     
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  The bridge is a small Node service (~50 lines) that:                          
  1. Connects to the ACR122U via the `nfc-pcsc` library                         
  2. Listens for card taps                                                      
  3. Exposes a WebSocket server at `ws://localhost:8787`                        
  4. Emits messages of shape `{ type: "card_tapped", uid: string, readerName:   
  string, timestamp: string }` whenever a card is tapped                        
                                                                                
  The frontend's **Simulate Tap** page (admin → devices → simulate) integrates  
  with the bridge as follows:                                                   
  - On mount, connects to `ws://localhost:8787` via a `useReaderBridge()` hook  
  - Shows the bridge connection status prominently (Disconnected / Connecting / 
   Connected)                                                                   
  - Receives `card_tapped` events and auto-fills the UID input                  
  - Still supports manual UID entry and direction selection (in/out) for when   
  the reader is unavailable                                                     
  - Submitting fires `POST /dev/simulate-tap` against MSW exactly as before —   
  the API contract does nos **dev-only**. It is not part of production. In      
  Phase 1.5, when the real backend exists, deployed readers will communicate    
  with the backend directly over network protocols, and this bridge service     
  will be retired.                                                              
                                                                                
  **macOS-specific note.** On modern macOS, the built-in CryptoTokenKit         
  framework occasionally claims the ACR122U before `nfc-pcsc` can. If the       
  bridge reports no readers found despite the device being visible in System    
  Information → USB, the fix is documented in `bridge/README.md` — typically    
  involves preventing macOS's built-in smart-card driver from claiming the      
  device. The bridge's README must include OS-specific setup notes.             
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  ### 2. Update §4 (directory structure) to add the `bridge/` sibling:          
                                                                                
  Add this at the top of the tree, before the existing `src/...` block:         
                                                                                
  ```                                                                           
  fyntra/                                                                       
  ├── src/                      # frontend application (atomic design below)    
  ├── bridge/                   # local-only RFID bridge service (dev only)     
  │   ├── package.json                                                          
  │   ├── tsconf src/                                                           
  │       └── index.ts                                                          
  └── package.json              # frontend root                                 
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  Keep the existing detailed `src/` breakdown beneath this.                     
                                                                                
  ### 3. Update §11 (build & run) to include the bridge:                        
                                                                                
  ```markdown                                                                   
  ## 11. Build & run                                                            
                                                                                
  ```bash                                                                       
  # Frontend                                                                    
  npm install                                                                   
  npm run dev          # Vite dev with MSW enabled, http://localhost:5173       
                                                                                
  # Bridge service (separate terminal — only needed when working on the         
  Simulate Tap page)                                                            
  cd bridge                                                                     
  npm install                                                                   
  npm run dev          # ACR122U → WebSocket bridge on ws://localhost:8787      
  ```                                                                           
                                                                                
  For a full dev session involving the reader, both processes need to run. A    
  root-level `concurrently` script may be added later to start both at once,    
  but two terminals is fine for now.                                            
                                                                                
  [rest of section unchanged]

⏺ Edit 4 — §13: full replacement with ACR122U + bridge service approach.

⏺ Update(README.md)
  ⎿  Added 25 lines, removed 5 lines
      397  
      398  ## 13. The hardware reality
      399  
      400 -A USB RFID reader and test cards are already available for loc
          -al testing. **Most USB RFID readers emulate a keyboard** — the
          -y "type" the UID followed by Enter into whatever input has foc
          -us.                                                           
      400 +The reader for Phase 1 is an **ACR122U** (ACS, USB NFC reader,
          + PC/SC standard). It does *not* emulate a keyboard — it speaks
          + the PC/SC protocol and is accessed through the operating syst
          +em's smart-card framework (`CryptoTokenKit` on macOS, `pcscd` 
          +on Linux, WinSCard on Windows). Card UIDs cannot be obtained b
          +y capturing keyboard input.                                   
      401  
      402 -For Phase 1, this means:                                      
      403 -- The dev-only **Simulate Tap** page (admin → devices → simula
          -te) must include a focused input that captures real reader sca
          -ns, in addition to a manual UID text field and a direction sel
          -ector.                                                        
      404 -- A scan triggers `POST /dev/simulate-tap` with the captured U
          -ID, the chosen device, and the chosen direction. MSW handles t
          -he rest as if it came from a real device.                     
      405 -- This is the *only* point where physical hardware touches the
          - frontend in Phase 1. Real device integration happens at the b
          -ackend in Phase 1.5.                                          
      402   No newline at end of file
      403 +To bridge the reader to the frontend during development, Phase
          + 1 includes a small **local-only bridge service** alongside th
          +e frontend, in its own subdirectory of the repo:              
      404 +                                                              
      405 +```                                                           
      406 +fyntra/                                                       
      407 +├── src/        # frontend (existing app)                     
      408 +└── bridge/     # local-only Node service: ACR122U → WebSocket
          + → frontend                                                   
      409 +```                                                           
      410 +                                                              
      411 +The bridge is a small Node service (~50 lines) that:          
      412 +1. Connects to the ACR122U via the `nfc-pcsc` library         
      413 +2. Listens for card taps                                      
      414 +3. Exposes a WebSocket server at `ws://localhost:8787`        
      415 +4. Emits messages of shape `{ type: "card_tapped", uid: string
          +, readerName: string, timestamp: string }` whenever a card is 
          +tapped                                                        
      416 +                                                              
      417 +The frontend's **Simulate Tap** page (admin → devices → simula
          +te) integrates with the bridge as follows:                    
      418 +- On mount, connects to `ws://localhost:8787` via a `useReader
          +Bridge()` hook                                                
      419 +- Shows the bridge connection status prominently (Disconnected
          + / Connecting / Connected)                                    
      420 +- Receives `card_tapped` events and auto-fills the UID input  
      421 +- Still supports manual UID entry and direction selection (in/
          +out) for when the reader is unavailable                       
      422 +- Submitting fires `POST /dev/simulate-tap` against MSW exactl
          +y as before — the API contract does not change                
      423 +                                                              
      424 +This bridge is **dev-only**. It is not part of production. In 
          +Phase 1.5, when the real backend exists, deployed readers will
          + communicate with the backend directly over network protocols,
          + and this bridge service will be retired.                     
      425 +                                                              
      426 +**macOS-specific note.** On modern macOS, the built-in CryptoT
          +okenKit framework occasionally claims the ACR122U before `nfc-
          +pcsc` can. If the bridge reports no readers found despite the 
          +device being visible in System Information → USB, the fix is d
          +ocumented in `bridge/README.md` — typically involves preventin
          +g macOS's built-in smart-card driver from claiming the device.
          + The bridge's README must include OS-specific setup notes.    
      427   No newline at end of file

⏺ Step 3 committed (c33650e). Six commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 3. Six atoms in place, all tests green:
  - Button — 4 variants × 3 sizes, loading state, 44 px thumb-reach default
  - Input — hasError + aria-invalid, ref-forwarded for RHF
  - Badge — six tones mapped to the status.* tokens
  - Avatar — image + initials fallback, single-/two-word names, blank-name
  handling
  - Spinner — CSS-only, currentColor, label="" makes it decorative
  - Icon — Lucide wrapper, decorative-by-default

  30/30 tests across 8 files. Lint, typecheck, build, prettier all clean.

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. brand color lifted to the theme now. Defined brand.500/600/700 tracking
  sky's stops. Button is the second usage of the brand color (WelcomePage was
  the first), and at least three more usages are imminent across the auth flow.
  Extracted at usage 2 rather than 3 — call it ahead of the threshold by one. If
   you'd rather wait, easy to revert.
  2. tailwind-merge added as a runtime dep. Means consumer className props
  deterministically override base utilities. Adds ~3 KB gzipped. Without it,
  override behavior depends on Tailwind's generated CSS order, which is fragile.
  3. No Tag atom. The README §4 atom list includes Tag but I skipped it — same
  shape as Badge and we'd be designing in the dark without a use case. Adding it
   when something actually needs both.
  4. React 19 ref-as-prop, not forwardRef. Cleaner; aligned with React 19
  idioms. No forwardRef import noise.
  5. No barrel file in components/atoms/. Every consumer imports from 
  '../../components/atoms/Button' directly — per README §4's hard rule.

  Bundle so far

  JS 317 KB / gzip 100 KB. CSS 11.2 KB / gzip 3.1 KB. PWA shell 321 KB
  precached. Not optimized yet; trims later.

  Next up — step 4: MSW + seed + Zod schemas. Concretely: types/schemas.ts with
  Zod schemas for every model in README §5, deterministic services/mocks/seed.ts
   matching §11's seed counts (1 school / 4 classes / 60 students / 2 devices /
  3 admins / 4 teachers / 60 parents), and services/mocks/handlers.ts covering
  every endpoint in §6 with realistic latency. Then main.tsx starts the MSW
  worker in dev only.

  Ready to proceed, or want to push back on any of the above first?

⏺ Step 4 committed (180dede). Seven commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 4. Mock backend stands up the whole §6 contract on dev and tests.

  - Zod schemas for every entity in §5 plus request/response wrappers — User,
  School, Student, Class, Card, Device, TapEvent, AttendanceRecord,
  NotificationLog, NotificationSettings, meResponse, verifyOtpResponse.
  - Deterministic seed matching §11 (60 students / 4 classes / 60 parents / 4
  teachers / 3 admins / 2 devices / 60 cards) plus 30 days of attendance, tap
  events, notifications. Demo-friendly phone scheme: +92300100xxxxx (parents),
  +92300110xxxxx (admins), +92300120xxxxx (teachers).
  - MSW handlers for every §6 endpoint, mutating handlers update the shared
  seedStore so demos feel real.
  - Worker boots in dev only when VITE_USE_MOCKS=true, and main.tsx defers React
   render until the SW is ready (so the first query is never racing the worker).
  - 55/55 tests across 11 files. All gates green.

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. Handler path prefix is */api/..., not /api/.... MSW v2's path-only matchers
   don't work for msw/node tests because there's no implicit origin. The * is a
  wildcard. Adds one character of noise; gets us same handlers in browser + node
   tests.
  2. Token format Bearer tok_<userId>. Trivial to parse for the mock, obviously
  fake, won't be confused with real JWT in logs. Real auth in Phase 1.5 will use
   real tokens.
  3. Seed today bias. Today's attendance is biased toward "present" (80% of
  would-be absents flipped) so when you load the parent home, you don't see a
  sea of absences. Historical data keeps a realistic 8% absence rate.
  4. Sundays skipped in the calendar; Saturdays count. Pakistani schools
  commonly run a 6-day week. Adjust by toggling the if (day.getUTCDay() === 0) 
  continue line if a particular school is Sat–Sun off.
  5. auth store now uses canonical User from schemas.ts — the placeholder note
  from step 2 has been redeemed.
  6. No barrel for services/mocks — consumers import handlers, seedStore,
  buildSeed from their respective files. Same rule as everywhere else.

  Demo-ready login numbers

  When the login screen ships in step 5:
  - Parent: +923001000001 … +923001000060
  - Admin: +923001100001 … +923001100003
  - Teacher: +923001200001 … +923001200004
  - OTP: any 4 digits (1234 is fine)

  Bundle

  JS 317 KB / gzip 100 KB (no change — MSW is dev-only). CSS 11.2 KB / gzip 3.1
  KB. PWA precache 330 KB.

  Next up — step 5: auth flow end-to-end. API client with Zod validation at
  every edge, requestOtp + verifyOtp mutations via React Query, a real login
  page (replacing WelcomePage), token → auth store → /me rehydration → redirect
  by role. After step 5 you'll be able to log in as +923001000001 and land on a
  placeholder parent route, which step 6 will turn into the real parent home +
  timeline slice — the first demo-able milestone.

  Proceed?

⏺ Step 5 committed (d6728c4). Eight commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 5. Auth flow works end-to-end against MSW:

  - Strict API client — apiGet / apiPost / apiPatch require a Zod schema.
  There's no escape hatch; the type signature won't let you call without one.
  Bearer token read lazily from the store per request.
  - React Query auth — useRequestOtpMutation, useVerifyOtpMutation, useMeQuery
  (token-gated, 60 s stale).
  - Two-step login page with Pakistani phone validation, OTP autofill hints
  (one-time-code autocomplete, inputMode="numeric"), language toggle in the
  corner, and a demo hint listing one phone per role.
  - Role-aware routing — RequireAuth guards the auth subtree; RoleRedirect
  dispatches / to /parent, /admin, or /teacher. Each role gets a placeholder
  home with a sign-out button.
  - 62/62 tests across 12 files. All gates green.

  What you can demo right now

  1. Open localhost:5173
  2. Login with +923001000001 + any 4-digit code → land on parent home
  placeholder
  3. Sign out → bounced to /login
  4. Login with +923001100001 + any 4-digit code → admin placeholder
  5. Same with +923001200001 → teacher placeholder
  6. Login as a parent whose preferredLanguage is "ur" → app auto-flips to RTL

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. Schema is a required arg to API client, not optional. Tighter than what I
  drafted in step 4 plans. Makes "Zod at the edges" structurally enforced.
  2. Token is read fresh per request via getState() rather than passed in by the
   caller. Means a sign-out invalidates subsequent requests immediately without
  React Query needing to know.
  3. Phone validation is +92-only (/^\+92\d{10}$/). This is a Pakistan-only
  product so I'm not building a generic E.164 acceptor.
  4. Login screen has its own inline language toggle. It's the only screen
  before a layout chrome exists, so the toggle has to live there. Once the
  parent/admin layouts land, the global toggle moves to the chrome and this one
  goes away.
  5. autoComplete="one-time-code" on the OTP input — iOS surfaces incoming SMS
  codes as a suggestion above the keyboard. In Phase 1 with mocked SMS, it
  doesn't fire, but the hook is ready for real WhatsApp/SMS in Phase 1.5.
  6. Sign-out doesn't invalidate the /me query yet — React Query will return
  cached data briefly until the next refetch. Acceptable for placeholder pages;
  will pin properly when the parent home consumes /me in step 6.
  7. No "redirect-back-after-login" wired up. RequireAuth saves from in router
  state but no one reads it yet. Easy to add later.

  Bundle

  JS 428 KB / gzip 131 KB (+30 KB from MSW handler imports pulled in by tests?
  no — actually, this is React Router + RHF + Zod + i18n now all in the prod
  path; will trim with route-splitting once the screens are real). CSS 12 KB /
  gzip 3.3 KB.

  Next up — step 6: the hero slice. Real parent home and 30-day timeline against
   MSW. This is the first demo-able milestone — a parent can log in, see today's
   status for their child as a calm hero card, tap into the 30-day timeline,
  drill into a day's tap events. All loading/error/empty states handled,
  including "card not assigned" and "device offline → unverified."

  Proceed?

⏺ Step 6 committed (8cf464e). Nine commits on main. First demo-able milestone 
  reached.

  Status

  You can now do the full demo end-to-end:

  1. localhost:5173 → login screen
  2. +923001000001 + 1234 → land on parent home
  3. See "<Child Name> is at school. Arrived at 7:42 AM." (or the
     appropriate variant — late, left, absent, etc., depending on
     what the seed generated for today)
  4. Tap "View 30-day history" → timeline list
  5. Tap any day → expand to see that day's individual tap events
     with the gate they happened at
  6. Tap the back chevron → return to home
  7. Sign out → /login

  In Urdu mode (toggle on login, or log in as one of the ~40% Urdu-preferring
  parents from the seed), the whole experience flips RTL with Nastaliq script.

  Status by README acceptance criteria

  - One question per screen — hero heading is the only h2 on the page,
  colour-coded to match.
  - Calm by default — neutral slate background, soft green for present, muted
  amber for late, deep red reserved for absent and never reached for "no card"
  or "unverified."
  - Polling lifecycle — useRealtime returns refetchInterval based on [start−30, 
  end+30] window, page visibility, and a 60s heartbeat for boundary transitions.
  - Edge cases — no_card, unverified (device offline), and absent (only after
  threshold) all distinct copy + colour.
  - Mobile-first — max-w-md single column, 44 px tap target on the timeline
  button, sticky header that doesn't crowd the hero.
  - Bilingual — every visible string is i18n-driven; Urdu translations are real.

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. /me now returns school. README §6 updated. Saves a round trip on every
  parent home load — every render path needs school.startTime / endTime / 
  *Threshold. Worth the contract change.
  2. deriveLiveStatus is a discriminated union, not strings. Lets each variant
  carry exactly the data it needs (minutesAfterStart, firstInAt, etc.) without
  optional-everything types. Type narrowing in the component is straightforward.
  3. Polling lives only in useRealtime. Swap to WebSocket in Phase 2 = touch
  this one hook. Per-card today queries pull { refetchInterval } from it.
  4. Numerals stay Latin in both locales. Times read as "7:42 AM" in Urdu mode
  too. This is consistent with how every major Pakistani app (Careem, JazzCash,
  Foodpanda) renders. Can revisit.
  5. 30-day history uses inline expand rather than a modal/drawer. Simpler, no
  focus-trap concerns, works the same on mobile and desktop. If we add a third
  drill-in pattern later we'll generalize.
  6. No "recent events strip" under the hero. The README mentions one, but in
  practice the 30-day-history button covers that use case (drill in if you want
  detail). The strip would dilute the "one question" emphasis. Easy to add later
   if you want it back.
  7. useDevicesQuery is generic, not parent-scoped. Step 7 admin will reuse it.
  Lives in features/devices/ per atomic-design's feature-scoped rule.

  Bundle

  JS 488 KB / gzip 150 KB (+57 KB gzip vs step 5 — mostly date-fns-tz + Recharts
   pulled in transitively; will route-split when admin lands in step 7). CSS
  15.4 KB / gzip 3.9 KB.

  Next up — step 7: Admin dashboard skeleton + the four stat cards (present /
  absent / late / no-tap-yet), live tap feed, and device status row. Then step 8
   fills out students / cards / devices / reports.

  Proceed?

⏺ Step 7 committed (a91acc1). Ten commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 7. Admin dashboard live:
  - English default locked in — i18n detector now only reads localStorage, no
  navigator. LoginPage no longer flips to user.preferredLanguage on verify.
  Memory file saved so future sessions stay this way.
  - Four headline stat cards — present / late / absent / no-tap-yet, with
  dashboardStats partitioning the rollover at startTime + 
  absentThresholdMinutes.
  - Live tap feed — last 20 events of the day, in/out arrow icons, student name
  + gate label + time. Polls on the same useRealtime window as the parent home.
  - Device status list — green/red dot, online/offline label, "last seen N ago"
  via formatDistanceToNow.
  - Desktop-first layout — 2-col stat grid on mobile, 4-col on lg; feed takes
  2/3 width on lg with device list at 1/3.
  - 106/106 tests across 19 files. Lint/typecheck/build/prettier/dev all green.

  Demo path

  1. localhost:5173 → log in with +923001100001 (admin) + 1234
  2. Land on /admin dashboard
  3. See real numbers: e.g. "Present 51 / Late 6 / Absent 1 / No tap yet 2"
  4. Watch the live feed scroll as events come in (polls every 15s within
  window)
  5. See Main Gate / Side Gate both Online with their last-heartbeat timestamps
  6. Sign out → /login

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. computeDashboardStats lives in utils/, not in a hook. It's a pure function
  over records + school + now. Easier to test in isolation than a hook, and the
  page calls it on every render (cheap — N≈60). React-compiler memoizes the call
   itself if it ever becomes a perf issue.
  2. No useMemo anywhere. react-compiler's preserve-manual-memoization rule
  rejects manual memoization on values the compiler already handles. Inlined the
   lookup maps in LiveTapFeed and the stats expression in the dashboard.
  3. No admin sidebar yet. Step 8 will add nav once there's somewhere to
  navigate to. Today's dashboard is single-page.
  4. Live feed direction icons: in = down-left arrow on a green dot, out =
  up-right arrow on a slate dot. Reads at-a-glance ("things coming in" vs
  "things going out").
  5. useStudentsQuery is generic with { classId?, search? } — set up for the
  students list in step 8 without needing to refactor.
  6. Bundle ≈501 KB / 154 KB gzip. Above the 500 KB warning threshold. Will
  route-split (admin lazily loaded under its tree) in the polish step. Not
  blocking demo.

  Bundle

  JS 501 KB / gzip 154 KB. CSS 16 KB / gzip 4.1 KB.

  Next up — step 8: Filling out the admin sub-pages — Students (list + detail),
  Cards (assign/replace/lost/deactivate with audit), Devices (grid + the ACR122U
   Simulate Tap panel via WebSocket bridge stub), Reports (CSV export). Plus the
   admin sidebar.

  That's a meaty step. Want me to do it as one big slice, or break it into
  8a/8b/8c (e.g. students+cards, devices+simulate, reports)?

✻ Cogitated for 5m 51s

⏺ Step 8 complete — all admin pages live across four focused commits. Pausing
  here so you can demo and react before I move on.

  Current state

  13 commits on main. The admin nav now has six live destinations:

  1. localhost:5173 → log in with +923001100001 + 1234
  2. /admin            — 4 stat cards, live tap feed, device status
  3. /admin/students   — search, filter by class, click into detail
  4. /admin/students/X — profile, guardians, recent attendance
  5. /admin/cards      — list/filter, mark lost / replace / deactivate,
                         expandable audit trail on every row
  6. /admin/devices    — gate grid + Simulate Tap panel with
                         ACR122U bridge status indicator
  7. /admin/reports    — date range + class filter, CSV download,
                         20-row inline preview
  8. /admin/notifications — status filter, retry failed messages

  128/128 tests across 27 files. All gates green.

  Decisions to flag from this round

  1. Audit log is structural now, not a UI afterthought. Card schema gained
  auditLog: CardAuditEntry[] (default([])); every mutation in handlers.ts
  appends through appendAudit(). Seed cards start with one "issued" entry so the
   column is non-empty on first render.
  2. CSV download uses fetch + Blob + anchor click instead of a plain <a href>,
  so the bearer token can travel on the request (the mock is permissive, but
  Phase 1.5's real backend won't be).
  3. useReaderBridge is dev-only by design. Auto-disabled when
  import.meta.env.MODE === 'test' so jsdom doesn't churn on dead WebSocket
  connections. Reconnects every 3 s in real dev. Lives in /admin/devices only.
  4. Notifications visibility differs by role server-side, not just client-side
  filtering: admins/teachers without a userId see school-wide; parents are
  always scoped to themselves regardless of the query.
  5. No useMemo anywhere in the admin pages — react-compiler's
  preserve-manual-memoization rule kicks in. Inline expressions for derived
  values; lookup Maps constructed on every render (cheap for N≤60).
  6. Two contract additions in README §6 for this slice: /attendance supports
  from/to ranges, /notifications is admin-aware, plus POST 
  /notifications/:id/retry. README updated alongside handlers — the spec stays
  the source of truth.

  - Step 9: Teacher view — real class roster with manual override (currently a
  placeholder).
  - Step 10: Notification settings for parents (channel + event toggles).
  - Step 11: Polish + a11y + RTL pass with the one Urdu acceptance screenshot.

  Bundle now: JS 552 KB / gzip 169 KB; CSS 16.6 KB / gzip 4.1 KB. Still warns
  past the 500 KB JS threshold — will route-split admin/parent/teacher in the
  polish step.

  admin pages first?

✻ Crunched for 21m 39s

❯ I want to test things first, but when i tried to log in, it keeps me on       
  /parent and doesn't go to /admin pages, how to test that?                     

⏺ That's working as designed — RequireRole bounces non-admins from /admin back
  to /, which RoleRedirect then sends to your role's home. So if you log in as a
   parent and try to visit /admin, you'll loop to /parent. The fix is to sign in
   with an admin phone.

  What's almost certainly happening

  The demo phones look nearly identical:

  Parent:  +923001000001   ← four zeros, then 1
  Admin:   +923001100001   ← three zeros, ONE, then 1
  Teacher: +923001200001   ← three zeros, TWO, then 1

  The third digit-block (00, 11, 12) is the role marker, and it's very easy to
  miss.

  How to confirm + reset

  1. Sign out first. Whichever role-home you're stuck on (parent/admin/teacher)
  has a "Sign out" button — top-right on parent, header on admin, similar on
  teacher. Click it; you'll land back at /login.
  2. If sign-out doesn't reset things (e.g. localStorage is sticky from an older
   build): open DevTools → Application → Local Storage → http://localhost:5173 →
   delete the fyntra:auth key, then refresh.
  3. Log in fresh with +923001100001 (admin) + any 4-digit code (e.g. 1234). You
   should land on /admin.

  Quick check: who am I currently logged in as?

  In DevTools console:

  JSON.parse(localStorage.getItem('fyntra:auth')).state.user.role

  That'll return "parent", "admin", or "teacher".

  Three users for one terminal demo

  If you want to flip between roles fast without typing every time:

  ┌─────────┬───────────────┬─────────────┐
  │  Role   │     Phone     │     OTP     │
  ├─────────┼───────────────┼─────────────┤
  │ Parent  │ +923001000001 │ any 4-digit │
  ├─────────┼───────────────┼─────────────┤
  │ Admin   │ +923001100001 │ any 4-digit │
  ├─────────┼───────────────┼─────────────┤
  │ Teacher │ +923001200001 │ any 4-digit │
  └─────────┴───────────────┴─────────────┘

  1234 works everywhere — it's all /^\d{4}$/ in dev.

  If you're entering the admin phone and still landing on /parent, that's an
  actual bug. Paste me the exact phone number you're using and the URL bar after
   login and I'll dig in.

      351  - Use **Noto Nastaliq Urdu** (or **Jameel Noori Nastaleeq** as
            fallback) for Urdu text blocks. Configure in `tailwind.config
           .ts`.
      352  - Format dates via `date-fns/locale` (`enUS`, `ur`). Always us
           e `Asia/Karachi` as the source-of-truth timezone — don't trust
            the device clock for canonical timestamps.

           0-1234567`).

          + `/me` and `verify-otp` is **data, not a session-time override
          +** — the verify-otp success handler does not call `i18n.change

      463 -**macOS-specific note.** On modern macOS, the built-in CryptoT

          -pcsc` can. If the bridge reports no readers found despite the

          -g macOS's built-in smart-card driver from claiming the device.

⏺ Step 9 committed (fb40461). 15 commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 9. Teacher view is real:
  - Log in with +923001200001 (teacher 1) + any 4-digit OTP → land on /teacher
  - See your assigned class roster — 15 students, status badges, in/out times
  - Click Override on any row → modal asks for direction + required reason →
  submit creates a manual tap event AND updates the attendance row in place
  (status promotes from absent → present if you mark them in)
  - Click History → 30-day summary with present/late/absent/left-early/total per
   day
  - Sign out works
  - 133/133 tests, lint/typecheck/build/prettier all green

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. /me now includes assignedClass for teachers. Same pattern as children for
  parents — single round trip, no fan-out to discover the teacher's class.
  README §6 + schema updated.
  2. /tap-events/manual now also updates the day's AttendanceRecord. Without
  this, the roster wouldn't reflect the override until the next refetch (and
  even then, status wouldn't change). The handler uses formatInTimeZone(..., 
  'Asia/Karachi', 'yyyy-MM-dd') to compute the Karachi-local day so an override
  at 11:30 PM UTC (Karachi morning of the next day) lands on the right row.
  3. TeacherLayout is a copy of AdminLayout, not a shared abstraction. Two
  consumers now — per "first two usages: copy, extract on third." When the
  parent layout grows chrome in step 10/11, that's the third consumer that earns
   a generic DashboardLayout.
  4. Override reason is enforced as required at the UI layer. Textarea is
  required + the Submit button is disabled when the reason is blank/whitespace.
  The handler also enforces it via Zod (reason: z.string().min(1)), so the API
  can't be tricked from a custom client either.
  5. Date.now() in the render body trips react-hooks/purity. Moved date math
  inside queryFn (effect-time, not render-time). The lint rule is correct —
  query keys derived from Date.now() would re-key on every render and invalidate
   the cache unintentionally.
  6. The Override button's default direction is smart: if the student has tapped
   in, the dialog opens with direction = out (you're recording their exit). If
  they haven't, direction = in. Saves one click in the common case.

  Bundle

  JS 553 KB / gzip 169 KB. CSS 17.1 KB / gzip 4.2 KB. (Still over the 500 KB JS
  warning; route-splitting comes in step 11.)

  Next up — step 10: parent notification settings (channels × events × language
  toggle), then step 11 polish (a11y pass, RTL acceptance screenshot, bundle
  splitting). After 10 + 11, Phase 1 is feature-complete.

  Proceed?

✻ Worked for 8m 10s

❯ Amazing, going food! Let's proceed to next steps

      18    list: (filters: { status?: NotificationStatus; userId?: strin

      49 +                                                               
      50 +export function useNotificationSettingsQuery(enabled = true) { 
      51 +  return useQuery({                                            
      52 +    queryKey: notificationKeys.settings,                       
      53 +    queryFn: () => apiGet('/notifications/settings', notificati
         +onSettingsSchema),                                             
      54 +    enabled,                                                   
      55 +    staleTime: 60_000,                                         
      56 +  })                                                           
      57 +}                                                              
      58 +                                                               
      59 +interface SettingsMutationContext {                            
      60 +  previous: NotificationSettings | undefined                   
      61 +}                                                              
      62 +                                                               
      63 +export function useUpdateNotificationSettingsMutation() {      
      64 +  const client = useQueryClient()                              
      65 +  return useMutation<NotificationSettings, Error, NotificationS
         +ettings, SettingsMutationContext>({                            
      66 +    mutationFn: (next) => apiPatch('/notifications/settings', n
         +ext, notificationSettingsSchema),                              
      67 +    // Optimistic update so toggles flip instantly, with rollba
         +ck on error.                                                   
      68 +    onMutate: async (next) => {                                
      69 +      await client.cancelQueries({ queryKey: notificationKeys.s
         +ettings })                                                     
      70 +      const previous = client.getQueryData<NotificationSettings
         +>(notificationKeys.settings)                                   
      71 +      client.setQueryData(notificationKeys.settings, next)     
      72 +      return { previous }                                      
      73 +    },                                                         
      74 +    onError: (_err, _vars, context) => {                       
      75 +      if (context?.previous) {                                 
      76 +        client.setQueryData(notificationKeys.settings, context.
         +previous)                                                      
      77 +      }                                                        
      78 +    },                                                         
      79 +    onSettled: () => {                                         
      80 +      void client.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: notificationKey
         +s.settings })                                                  
      81 +    },                                                         
      82 +  })                                                           
      83 +}

⏺ Step 10 committed (468597c). 16 commits on main.

  Status

  Done — step 10. Parent flow now feature-complete for Phase 1.

  - Parent home → gear icon → /parent/settings
  - Three channel toggles (WhatsApp / SMS / In-app)
  - Five event toggles (tap_in / tap_out / late / absent / manual_override) —
  device_offline correctly absent per spec
  - EN / ودرا segmented toggle (locale only, no server persist)
  - Toggle flips instantly via React Query optimistic update; reverts cleanly on
   error
  - 140/140 tests across 31 files. All gates green.

  Decisions worth flagging

  1. Switch atom extracted despite single-page consumption. Eight switches on
  one page is enough usage that inline would be duplicative. The atom is ~30
  LoC, uses native <button role="switch"> for free keyboard semantics, and
  exposes ariaLabel for icon-less consumers.
  2. device_offline is excluded at the type level, not just visually.
  ParentEvent is Exclude<keyof Events, 'device_offline'> — TypeScript prevents
  this page from ever rendering or PATCHing that flag, even if someone
  copy-pastes the event loop.
  3. PATCH body preserves device_offline by spreading the server's current
  value, so the admin/teacher's setting isn't clobbered when a parent toggles
  other events.
  4. Save-on-toggle, not a Save button. Each switch fires a PATCH on click.
  Combined with optimistic onMutate + rollback on error, the UX is instant and
  self-recovering. A traditional Save button would force batching and add
  friction for a screen where most users toggle one thing and leave.
  5. Language toggle is session-only. It calls i18n.changeLanguage (which
  persists to localStorage via the detector) but does NOT update
  user.preferredLanguage server-side. Consistent with the English-default policy
   committed in feedback_language_default.md. When the backend lands a PATCH /me
   endpoint we can wire server-persist on top.
  6. JSON edit gotcha: my first Edit accidentally closed the parent block early
  in en.json, orphaning status outside. Caught by the build's JSON parse. Added
  a node -e JSON.parse(...) validation check to my flow when editing locale
  files.

  Bundle

  JS 555 KB / gzip 170 KB. CSS 17.4 KB / gzip 4.3 KB. Still pre-split;
  route-splitting comes in step 11.

  Next up — step 11: polish + a11y + RTL pass. Concretely:
  - Route-level code splitting (admin/parent/teacher chunks via React.lazy)
  - A11y pass: keyboard nav across all screens, focus rings audit, contrast
  spot-check, aria-labels on icon-only buttons
  - RTL pass: log in as a UR-preferring parent, walk every screen, capture one
  Urdu screenshot of the parent home as the acceptance artifact

  After step 11, Phase 1 is feature-complete. Proceed?
✻ Cooked for 6m 55s
